      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L788" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="788"></td>
        <td id="LC788" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">``Reproducibility is just collaboration with people you don&#39;t know,</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L789" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="789"></td>
        <td id="LC789" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">including yourself next week&#39;&#39;---Philip Stark, University of California Berkeley Statistics</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L790" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="790"></td>
        <td id="LC790" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\end</span>{quote}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L791" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="791"></td>
        <td id="LC791" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L792" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="792"></td>
        <td id="LC792" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">Replication, in both practice and principle, is a key part of social</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L793" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="793"></td>
        <td id="LC793" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">science research. We first define what exactly we mean by replication</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L794" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="794"></td>
        <td id="LC794" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">using the taxonomy developed in <span class="pl-c1">\cite</span>{hamermesh_viewpoint:_2007} and <span class="pl-c1">\cite</span>{hunter_desperate_2001}.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L795" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="795"></td>
        <td id="LC795" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">According to Hamermesh, replication comes in a few different shapes: pure, statistical, and</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L796" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="796"></td>
        <td id="LC796" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">scientific.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L797" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="797"></td>
        <td id="LC797" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L798" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="798"></td>
        <td id="LC798" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\begin</span>{itemize}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L799" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="799"></td>
        <td id="LC799" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\item</span></td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L800" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="800"></td>
        <td id="LC800" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">  Pure: Using the exact same data and the exact same model to see if the</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L801" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="801"></td>
        <td id="LC801" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">  published results are reproduced exactly.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L802" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="802"></td>
        <td id="LC802" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\item</span></td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L803" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="803"></td>
        <td id="LC803" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">  Scientific: Using a different sample from a different population, and</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L804" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="804"></td>
        <td id="LC804" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">  similar, but perhaps not identical model .</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L805" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="805"></td>
        <td id="LC805" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\item</span></td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L806" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="806"></td>
        <td id="LC806" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">  Statistical: Using the same model and underlying population but a</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L807" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="807"></td>
        <td id="LC807" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">  different sample. In Hamermesh&#39;s view, this is less relevant to certain fields, such as economics,</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L808" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="808"></td>
        <td id="LC808" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">  where researchers are likely to already use as large a sample as is available.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L809" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="809"></td>
        <td id="LC809" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\end</span>{itemize}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L810" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="810"></td>
        <td id="LC810" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L811" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="811"></td>
        <td id="LC811" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">One might imagine a fourth type that uses the same data but probes the data using additional robustness and sensitivity checks. Others have described replication in terms of a spectrum from full replication (independent collection of data and re-running analysis) to</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L812" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="812"></td>
        <td id="LC812" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">reproducibility, where the same data and code are re-used by other</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L813" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="813"></td>
        <td id="LC813" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">researchers <span class="pl-c1">\citep</span>{peng_reproducible_2011}. Whatever the terminology used, replication or reproducibility, transparent research requires making data and code available to other researchers so they can try and get the same results.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L814" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="814"></td>
        <td id="LC814" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L815" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="815"></td>
        <td id="LC815" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L816" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="816"></td>
        <td id="LC816" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\subsection</span>{Code and Workflow}<span class="pl-c1">\label</span>{code-and-workflow}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L817" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="817"></td>
        <td id="LC817" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L818" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="818"></td>
        <td id="LC818" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">Reproducing research often involves using the exact code and statistical</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L819" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="819"></td>
        <td id="LC819" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">programming done by the original researcher. To make this possible, code</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L820" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="820"></td>
        <td id="LC820" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">needs to be both (1) easily available and (2) easily interpretable.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L821" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="821"></td>
        <td id="LC821" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">Thanks to several free and easy to use websites described below, code</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L822" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="822"></td>
        <td id="LC822" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">can easily be made available by researchers without requiring funding or</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L823" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="823"></td>
        <td id="LC823" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">website hosting. Making code easily interpretable is a somewhat more complicated</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L824" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="824"></td>
        <td id="LC824" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">task, nevertheless, the extra effort spent to make a more manageable</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L825" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="825"></td>
        <td id="LC825" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">code pays off with large dividends.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L826" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="826"></td>
        <td id="LC826" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L827" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="827"></td>
        <td id="LC827" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\subsubsection</span>{Publicly Sharing Code}<span class="pl-c1">\label</span>{publicly-sharing-code}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L828" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="828"></td>
        <td id="LC828" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L829" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="829"></td>
        <td id="LC829" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">Once analysis is complete (or even before this stage) researchers should</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L830" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="830"></td>
        <td id="LC830" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">share their data and code with the public. GitHub</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L831" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="831"></td>
        <td id="LC831" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">(<span class="pl-c1">\url</span>{http://www.github.com}), The Center for Open Science&#39;s Open</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L832" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="832"></td>
        <td id="LC832" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">Science Framework (<span class="pl-c1">\url</span>{http://osf.io}), and Harvard University&#39;s</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L833" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="833"></td>
        <td id="LC833" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">Dataverse (<span class="pl-c1">\url</span>{http://thedata.org}) are all free repositories for data</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L834" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="834"></td>
        <td id="LC834" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">and code that include easy to use version control.<span class="pl-c1">\footnote</span>{BitBucket</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L835" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="835"></td>
        <td id="LC835" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">  (<span class="pl-c1">\href</span>{styles.xml}{http://www.bitbucket.org}) is another</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L836" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="836"></td>
        <td id="LC836" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">  web service that one can use for free version control and archiving</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L837" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="837"></td>
        <td id="LC837" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">  of public data and code.} </td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L838" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="838"></td>
        <td id="LC838" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">  </td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L839" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="839"></td>
        <td id="LC839" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">Version control is a powerful way to archive versions of files so that old versions are not lost and can be returned</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L840" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="840"></td>
        <td id="LC840" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">to if needed. The most naive way to organize a project would be to just name a file ``MyAnalysis.do&#39;&#39; and then save over it any time you or your coauthor made changes. We sincerely hope no one is working this way, since you are losing tons of information. Most people are probably doing some version of the ``date and initials&#39;&#39; method. Instead of simply calling one&#39;s analysis code ``MyAnalysis.do&#39;&#39; and repeatedly saving over and losing old versions, when you save a new version, you add the date to the file name: ``MyAnalysis.2014.08.13.do&#39;&#39;, and if a co-author makes changes on the same day, they add their initials:``MyAnalysis.2014.08.13\_GC.do&#39;&#39; or they change the date: ``MyAnalysis.2014.08.14.do&#39;&#39;. This can work on small projects, but it really isn&#39;t the best way to work. Why does the operating system tell me the file from August 13 was modified in October? What if one analysis script file is called 14 times in 9 different files---did you remember to go through and update all the calls? \cite{GentzkowShapiro} provide strong evidence of the inadequacy of dating and initialing : ``\textit{Not one piece of commercial software you have on your PC, your phone, your tablet, your car, or any other modern computing device was written with the ``date and initial&#39;&#39; method.}&#39;&#39; [emphasis original]</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L841" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="841"></td>
        <td id="LC841" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L842" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="842"></td>
        <td id="LC842" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">The solution is version control (also referred to as revision control). Version control is free software (<span class="pl-c1">\href</span>{https://git-scm.com/book/en/v2/Getting-Started-About-Version-Control}{Git} and <span class="pl-c1">\href</span>{https://mercurial.selenic.com/}{Mercurial} are popular and free implementations) that stores all versions of files you create, and can easily compare versions of the files to highlight changes, revert to earlier versions, accept or reject changes proposed by a collaborator, and reconcile conflicting versions when different people make changes to the same file. Version control creates a repository, and stores all versions of your files in the repository<span class="pl-c1">\footnote</span>{Repositories can take up a significant amount of space, but you can avoid this problem by not storing generated files or binaries (.pdf, .docx, .etc) since every user with access to the repository should be able to recompile and generate files on their own. Version control works best with simple text files.}  Web services</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L843" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="843"></td>
        <td id="LC843" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">such as <span class="pl-c1">\href</span>{http:www.github.com}{GitHub} offer free hosting of these repositories with easy to use web-based interfaces and GUI software, so that you and your collaborators can all access the same files, but you can easily host the repository on a server of your own. </td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L844" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="844"></td>
        <td id="LC844" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L845" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="845"></td>
        <td id="LC845" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\subsubsection</span>{Managing Workflow}<span class="pl-c1">\label</span>{managing-workflow}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L846" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="846"></td>
        <td id="LC846" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L847" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="847"></td>
        <td id="LC847" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">Code is just one aspect of a larger structure we refer to as</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L848" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="848"></td>
        <td id="LC848" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">``workflow&#39;&#39; after <span class="pl-c1">\cite</span>{long_workflow_2008}, by which we mean the</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L849" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="849"></td>
        <td id="LC849" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">combination of data, code, organization, and documentation: everything</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L850" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="850"></td>
        <td id="LC850" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">from file and variable names to folder organization as well as efficient</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L851" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="851"></td>
        <td id="LC851" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">and readable programming, and data storage and documentation. We strongly recommend that Stata-users read <span class="pl-c1">\cite</span>{long_workflow_2008} and R users read <span class="pl-c1">\cite</span>{gandrud2013reproducible} for workflow recommendations both general and specific to their respective programming language<span class="pl-c1">\footnote</span>{Also see and <span class="pl-c1">\cite</span>{kirchkamp_workflow_????}}. Our suggestions here borrow heavily from their excellent work. </td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L852" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="852"></td>
        <td id="LC852" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L853" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="853"></td>
        <td id="LC853" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">Another excellent, more brief work is Matthew Gentzkow and Jesse Shapiro&#39;s excellent manual on code and data <span class="pl-c1">\href</span>{https://www.brown.edu/Research/Shapiro/pdfs/CodeAndData.pdf}{<span class="pl-c1">\citep</span>{GentzkowShapiro}}. They come from the same background as us--they didn&#39;t take many programming classes, they&#39;re just clever and figured it out. But once their data got massive, and their programming problems got massive with it, they figured they should listen to the fulltime programmers and database managers who had spent years and billions of dollars solving these problems. Their manual adapts many of these solutions to data-based social science research.   </td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L854" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="854"></td>
        <td id="LC854" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L855" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="855"></td>
        <td id="LC855" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">We also refer undergraduate instructors and others who may be interested to Richard Ball and Norm Medeiros&#39; <span class="pl-c1">\href</span>{http://www.haverford.edu/TIER/}{Project TIER} (Teaching Integrity in Empirical Research), which is a ``protocol for comprehensively documenting all the steps of data management and analysis that go into an empirical research paper.&#39;&#39; A specific file organization using the Open Science Framework is taught so that teachers can exactly reproduce the work of every student (and so students can reliably get the same answer every time they conduct their analysis). </td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L856" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="856"></td>
        <td id="LC856" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>

</td>

      <tr>
        <td id="L859" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="859"></td>
        <td id="LC859" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">Although we agree with the movement by many towards open source software such</td>

      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L861" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="861"></td>
        <td id="LC861" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">traditions of using proprietary software such as SAS and STATA, and</td>

        <td id="L862" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="862"></td>

      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L863" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="863"></td>
        <td id="LC863" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">task in researchers&#39; busy lives. That said, there are several general</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L864" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="864"></td>

      </tr>

</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L868" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="868"></td>
        <td id="LC868" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\paragraph</span>{Writing Code:}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L869" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="869"></td>
        <td id="LC869" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">Perhaps the most important rule is to write code instead of working by hand. By</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L870" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="870"></td>
        <td id="LC870" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">that we mean:</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L871" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="871"></td>

</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L872" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="872"></td>
        <td id="LC872" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\begin</span>{itemize}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L873" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="873"></td>
        <td id="LC873" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\item</span></td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L874" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="874"></td>
        <td id="LC874" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">  Do not modify data by hand, such as with a spreadsheet. Which is to</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L875" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="875"></td>
        <td id="LC875" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">  say, don&#39;t use Excel.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L876" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="876"></td>
        <td id="LC876" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\item</span></td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L877" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="877"></td>
        <td id="LC877" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">  Use neither the command line nor drop-down menus nor point-and-click</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L878" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="878"></td>
        <td id="LC878" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">  options in statistical software.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L879" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="879"></td>
        <td id="LC879" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\item</span></td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L880" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="880"></td>
        <td id="LC880" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">  Instead, do everything with scripts.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L881" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="881"></td>
        <td id="LC881" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\end</span>{itemize}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L882" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="882"></td>
        <td id="LC882" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L883" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="883"></td>
        <td id="LC883" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">The simple reason for this is reproducibility. Modifying data in Excel</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L884" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="884"></td>
        <td id="LC884" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">or any similar spreadsheet program leaves no record of the changes made</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L885" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="885"></td>
        <td id="LC885" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">to the data, nor any explanation of the reasoning or timing behind any</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L886" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="886"></td>
        <td id="LC886" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">changes. Although it may seem easy or quick to do a one-time-only</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L887" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="887"></td>
        <td id="LC887" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">cleaning of data in Excel, or make ``minor&#39;&#39; changes to get the data</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L888" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="888"></td>
        <td id="LC888" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">into a format readable by a researcher&#39;s preferred statistical software,</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L889" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="889"></td>
        <td id="LC889" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">unless these changes are written down in excruciating detail, this is</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L890" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="890"></td>
        <td id="LC890" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">not reproducible by other researchers. It is better to write a programming</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L891" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="891"></td>
        <td id="LC891" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">script that imports the raw data, does all necessary changes, with</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L892" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="892"></td>
        <td id="LC892" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">comments in the code that explain changes, and saves any intermediate</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L893" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="893"></td>
        <td id="LC893" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">data sets used in analysis. Then, researchers can share their initial</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L894" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="894"></td>
        <td id="LC894" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">raw data and their code, and other researchers can reproduce their work</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L895" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="895"></td>
        <td id="LC895" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">exactly.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L896" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="896"></td>
        <td id="LC896" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L897" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="897"></td>
        <td id="LC897" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">Though we understand that a fair amount of research has been done using</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L898" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="898"></td>
        <td id="LC898" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">pull down menus in SPSS or Stata, we advise against this. A bare minimum</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L899" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="899"></td>
        <td id="LC899" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">if one insists on going this route is to use the built-in</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L900" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="900"></td>
        <td id="LC900" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">command-logging features of the software. In Stata, this involves the</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L901" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="901"></td>
        <td id="LC901" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">`cmdlog&#39; command, in SPSS, this involves the paste button to add to a</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L902" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="902"></td>
        <td id="LC902" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">syntax.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L903" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="903"></td>
        <td id="LC903" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L904" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="904"></td>
        <td id="LC904" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">The ideal is to make everything, including changes like rounding and</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L905" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="905"></td>
        <td id="LC905" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">formatting, done with scripts. Even downloading of data from websites</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L906" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="906"></td>
        <td id="LC906" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">can be done through a script. For example, in R, the download.file()</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L907" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="907"></td>
        <td id="LC907" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">function can be used to save data from a website. (Though of course this</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L908" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="908"></td>
        <td id="LC908" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">opens the possibility to the data file changing. When reproducing</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L909" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="909"></td>
        <td id="LC909" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">results from a given dataset is more important than the data from a</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L910" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="910"></td>
        <td id="LC910" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">specific source, researchers should download their raw dataset once, and</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L911" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="911"></td>
        <td id="LC911" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">never save over it, instead saving all modified intermediate datasets in</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L912" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="912"></td>
        <td id="LC912" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">a separate location.) Another extremely important way to prevent</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L913" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="913"></td>
        <td id="LC913" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">unintentional changes to data is to always set the seed for random</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L914" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="914"></td>
        <td id="LC914" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">number generators whenever any random numbers are to be used (set.seed()</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L915" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="915"></td>
        <td id="LC915" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">in R, set seed () in Stata). Additionally, information about the exact</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L916" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="916"></td>
        <td id="LC916" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">software version used should be included (include the `version&#39; command in Stata, or use the</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L917" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="917"></td>
        <td id="LC917" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">session.info() command in R) as well as computer processor and operating</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L918" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="918"></td>
        <td id="LC918" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">system information. The casual programmer may assume that sophisticated</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L919" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="919"></td>
        <td id="LC919" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">software would always produce the exact same answer across multiple</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L920" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="920"></td>
        <td id="LC920" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">versions of software and platforms, but this is not the case. This is also definitely not the case with user-written packages. R users can use the packageVersion() command, and can run old versions of packages since they are archived at <span class="pl-c1">\href</span>{http://cran.r-project.org}{CRAN}. Stata users can use the viewsource command for any .ado they use, but since the Statistical Software Components (SSC) unfortunately does not archive old versions, reproducibility may be lost, so ideally researchers would include the actual code for the version of the user-written .ado along with their publicly archived data and code files</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L921" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="921"></td>
        <td id="LC921" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L922" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="922"></td>
        <td id="LC922" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L923" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="923"></td>
        <td id="LC923" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">Finally, two simple organizing principles to consider are:</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L924" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="924"></td>
        <td id="LC924" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\begin</span>{enumerate}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L925" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="925"></td>
        <td id="LC925" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\item</span> </td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L926" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="926"></td>
        <td id="LC926" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"> Consider not saving statistical output, and just saving the code and data that generates it. Obviously this would be unrealistically time consuming for large projects, but the idea is that you should be able to reproduce all steps of your analysis that you could in theory take this approach.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L927" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="927"></td>
        <td id="LC927" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L928" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="928"></td>
        <td id="LC928" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\item</span></td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L929" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="929"></td>
        <td id="LC929" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">What would happen if you, or your laptop hard drive, were hit by a bus? How easily would anyone else be able to reproduce your work? Hopefully the probability is non-zero.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L930" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="930"></td>
        <td id="LC930" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\end</span>{enumerate}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L931" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="931"></td>
        <td id="LC931" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L932" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="932"></td>
        <td id="LC932" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\subsection</span>{General Workflow</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L933" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="933"></td>
        <td id="LC933" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">Suggestions:}<span class="pl-c1">\label</span>{general-workflow-suggestions}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L934" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="934"></td>
        <td id="LC934" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">Here we offer some specific workflow organization suggestions that should be valid regardless of code or operating system.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L935" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="935"></td>
        <td id="LC935" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\begin</span>{itemize}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L936" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="936"></td>
        <td id="LC936" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\item</span></td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L937" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="937"></td>
        <td id="LC937" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">  Do not use spaces in directory or file names, as it complicates referring to them in certain software.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L938" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="938"></td>
        <td id="LC938" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\item</span></td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L939" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="939"></td>
        <td id="LC939" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">  Use ``naming directories&#39;&#39;, .i.e.~a directory beginning with ``-&#39;&#39; (so</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L940" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="940"></td>
        <td id="LC940" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">  that it will appear first alphabetically) inside each directory to</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L941" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="941"></td>
        <td id="LC941" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">  explain the contents of the above directory.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L942" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="942"></td>
        <td id="LC942" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\item</span></td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L943" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="943"></td>
        <td id="LC943" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">  Add name, date, and describe contents, as well as updates, to all</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L944" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="944"></td>
        <td id="LC944" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">  scripting files.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L945" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="945"></td>
        <td id="LC945" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\item</span></td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L946" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="946"></td>
        <td id="LC946" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">  Keep a daily research log, i.e. a detailed written diary of what research is done on a given day. You&#39;ll be surprised how often this will be useful to answer questions about whether you ran a certain test or not, when you did it, and what you called the file.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L947" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="947"></td>
        <td id="LC947" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">  </td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L948" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="948"></td>
        <td id="LC948" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\item</span></td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L949" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="949"></td>
        <td id="LC949" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">    Make sure that your script files are self-contained. That is, don&#39;t write a program that only works if you run a group of other files previously in a specific order and then leave things a certain precarious way. You should be able to run intermediate steps of the workflow without disrupting things downstream.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L950" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="950"></td>
        <td id="LC950" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"> </td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L951" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="951"></td>
        <td id="LC951" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\item</span></td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L952" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="952"></td>
        <td id="LC952" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">  You can never comment too much.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L953" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="953"></td>
        <td id="LC953" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\item</span></td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L954" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="954"></td>
        <td id="LC954" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">  Indent your code</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L955" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="955"></td>
        <td id="LC955" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\item</span></td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L956" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="956"></td>
        <td id="LC956" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">    Once you post/distribute code or data, any changes at all require a new file name.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L957" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="957"></td>
        <td id="LC957" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\item</span></td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L958" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="958"></td>
        <td id="LC958" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">  Separate your cleaning and analysis files; don&#39;t make any new variables</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L959" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="959"></td>
        <td id="LC959" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">  that need saving (or will be used by multiple analysis</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L960" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="960"></td>
        <td id="LC960" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">  files) in an analysis file---it is better to only create the variables once so you know they&#39;re the identical when used in different analysis files.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L961" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="961"></td>
        <td id="LC961" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\item</span></td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L962" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="962"></td>
        <td id="LC962" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">  Never name a file ``final&#39;&#39; because it won&#39;t be.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L963" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="963"></td>
        <td id="LC963" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\item</span></td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L964" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="964"></td>
        <td id="LC964" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">  Name binary variables ``male&#39;&#39; instead of ``gender&#39;&#39; so that the name is more informative. </td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L965" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="965"></td>
        <td id="LC965" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\item</span></td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L966" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="966"></td>
        <td id="LC966" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">  Use a prefix such as x<span class="pl-cce">\_</span> or temp<span class="pl-cce">\_</span> so you know which files can easily</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L967" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="967"></td>
        <td id="LC967" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">  be deleted.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L968" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="968"></td>
        <td id="LC968" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\item</span></td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L969" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="969"></td>
        <td id="LC969" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">  Never change the contents of a variable unless you give it a new name.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L970" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="970"></td>
        <td id="LC970" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\item</span></td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L971" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="971"></td>
        <td id="LC971" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">  Every variable should have a label.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L972" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="972"></td>
        <td id="LC972" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\end</span>{itemize}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L973" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="973"></td>
        <td id="LC973" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L974" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="974"></td>
        <td id="LC974" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\subsection</span>{Stata-specific</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L975" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="975"></td>
        <td id="LC975" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">Suggestions}<span class="pl-c1">\label</span>{stata-specific-suggestions}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L976" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="976"></td>
        <td id="LC976" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L977" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="977"></td>
        <td id="LC977" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\begin</span>{itemize}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L978" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="978"></td>
        <td id="LC978" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\item</span></td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L979" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="979"></td>
        <td id="LC979" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">  Use the full set of missing values available to you (``.a&#39;&#39;-``.z&#39;&#39;, not exclusively</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L980" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="980"></td>
        <td id="LC980" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">  ``.&#39;&#39;) in order to distinguish between ``don&#39;t know&#39;&#39; and ``didn&#39;t ask&#39;&#39; or other distinct reasons for missing data.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L981" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="981"></td>
        <td id="LC981" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\item</span></td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L982" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="982"></td>
        <td id="LC982" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">  Make sure code always produces same result---if you use anything randomly generated, set the seed. When sorting or merging, you need to be sure to uniquely specify observations, because if you don&#39;t, Stata does something arbitrary and not repeatable. So instead of just sorting or merging on `ID&#39; when there are multiple observations per ID, sort by `ID&#39; and `name.&#39; You can use the `duplicates&#39; command to test whether the <span class="pl-c1">\textit</span>{varlist} you use uniquely indentifies observations. The `sort, stable&#39; command can be used, though it is slower.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L983" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="983"></td>
        <td id="LC983" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\item</span></td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L984" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="984"></td>
        <td id="LC984" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">  Use the `version&#39; command in your .do file to ensure that other researchers who run your code with a newer version of Stata get the same results. </td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L985" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="985"></td>
        <td id="LC985" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\item</span></td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L986" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="986"></td>
        <td id="LC986" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">  Don&#39;t use abbreviations for variables (which may become unstable after</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L987" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="987"></td>
        <td id="LC987" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">  adding variables) or commands (beyond reason)</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L988" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="988"></td>
        <td id="LC988" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\item</span></td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L989" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="989"></td>
        <td id="LC989" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">  Avoid using global macros, and use locals instead. (This is a common piece of programming advice: since globals can be accessed across different functions or spaces, they can create contradictions or inconsistent dependencies. In Stata, it&#39;s possible they can be safely used to define directory paths so collaborators can work across different computers, but that should likely be the extent of their use.)</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L990" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="990"></td>
        <td id="LC990" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\item</span></td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L991" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="991"></td>
        <td id="LC991" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">  Use locals for varlists to ensure that long lists of variables include the same variables whenever intended.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L992" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="992"></td>
        <td id="LC992" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\item</span></td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L993" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="993"></td>
        <td id="LC993" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">  Use computer-stored versions of numerical output instead of manually typing in numbers or copying and pasting. For example, instead of copying and pasting the mean after a `summ&#39; command, refer to `r(mean)&#39;. Use the `return list&#39; command to see a full list of stored values after a regular command and the `ereturn list&#39; after estimation commands.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L994" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="994"></td>
        <td id="LC994" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\item</span></td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L995" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="995"></td>
        <td id="LC995" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">  If you have a master .do file that calls other .do files, which each have their own .log file, you can run</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L996" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="996"></td>
        <td id="LC996" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">  multiple log files at the same time (so you have a master .log file)</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L997" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="997"></td>
        <td id="LC997" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\item</span></td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L998" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="998"></td>
        <td id="LC998" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">  Use the `label data&#39; and `notes&#39; commands to label datasets and help yourself and other researchers easily identify the contents.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>

        <td id="LC1085" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">Econometrics, Journal of Business and Economic Statistics}) requested</td>
      </tr>

      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1114" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1114"></td>

</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1115" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1115"></td>
        <td id="LC1115" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">The previous section on the <span class="pl-c1">\emph</span>{JMCB} describes only a few journals in</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1116" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1116"></td>
        <td id="LC1116" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">one field of the social sciences. Even if the journal to which you</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1117" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1117"></td>
        <td id="LC1117" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">submit your research does not require you to supply them with your code</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1118" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1118"></td>
        <td id="LC1118" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">and data, researchers should still share these materials. Though some</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1119" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1119"></td>
        <td id="LC1119" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">repositories, particularly Harvard&#39;s Dataverse, seem equipped to handle</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1120" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1120"></td>
        <td id="LC1120" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">data from practically any researcher (a free 1 TB of storage is</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1121" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1121"></td>
        <td id="LC1121" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">standard, with more possible upon request), many repositories specialize. <span class="pl-c1">\href</span>{http://www.re3data.org}{The Registry of Research Data Repositories}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1122" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1122"></td>
        <td id="LC1122" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">has described over 900 data repositories to help you find the right data</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1123" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1123"></td>
        <td id="LC1123" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">repository for your data. A key advantage to using a trusted repository</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1124" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1124"></td>
        <td id="LC1124" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">such as one listed here, in lieu of simply throwing the data up on your</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1125" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1125"></td>
        <td id="LC1125" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">own website or making your Dropbox folder public, is that many of these</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1126" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1126"></td>
        <td id="LC1126" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">repositories will take your data in its proprietary (Stata, SAS, SPSS,</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1127" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1127"></td>
        <td id="LC1127" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">etc.) form, and make it accessible in other formats. Storing your data in a repository with other similar datasets also makes it easier for others to find your data, instead of requiring that they already know of its existence, as would likely be the case with personal websites. Your own personal website is also more likely to be taken offline, should a researcher change schools or retire.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1128" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1128"></td>
        <td id="LC1128" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1129" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1129"></td>
        <td id="LC1129" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\subsubsection</span>{Differential Privacy}<span class="pl-c1">\label</span>{differential-privacy}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1130" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1130"></td>
        <td id="LC1130" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1131" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1131"></td>
        <td id="LC1131" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">One important caveat to making data widely available, is that despite</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1132" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1132"></td>
        <td id="LC1132" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">anonymization, in the age of big data, sometimes individual subjects can</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1133" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1133"></td>
        <td id="LC1133" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">easily be identified. <span class="pl-c1">\cite</span>{heffetz_privacy_2014} recount deliberate data</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1134" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1134"></td>
        <td id="LC1134" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">releases by Yahoo! Inc., the Massachusetts state government, and</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1135" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1135"></td>
        <td id="LC1135" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">Netflix, that could easily be used to identify individuals in the data,</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1136" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1136"></td>
        <td id="LC1136" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">despite the absence of direct identifiers such as names or social</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1137" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1137"></td>
        <td id="LC1137" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">security numbers. The problem is that ``de-identification does not</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1138" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1138"></td>
        <td id="LC1138" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">guarantee anonymization.&#39;&#39; This problem is well known in computer science, but solutions are still being developed and are not widely implemented.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1139" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1139"></td>
        <td id="LC1139" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1140" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1140"></td>
        <td id="LC1140" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1141" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1141"></td>
        <td id="LC1141" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\subsection</span>{Reporting Standards}<span class="pl-c1">\label</span>{reporting-standards}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1142" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1142"></td>
        <td id="LC1142" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">In research, the devil truly is in the details. Whether it is for assessing the validity of a research design or for</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1143" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1143"></td>
        <td id="LC1143" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">attempting to replicate a study, details of what exactly was done must be recorded and made available to other researchers.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1144" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1144"></td>
        <td id="LC1144" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">The exact details that are relevant will likely differ from field to field, but an increasing number of fields have</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1145" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1145"></td>
        <td id="LC1145" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">produced centralized checklists that describe (in excruciating detail) what disclosure is required of published studies. These checklists are not often published with the paper, but can be submitted with the original article so that reviewers can check that it has been completed. With infinite and easy web storage, researchers can easily post these materials on their website even if journal editors insist on cutting their methods sections for space reasons. </td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1146" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1146"></td>
        <td id="LC1146" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1147" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1147"></td>
        <td id="LC1147" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\subsubsection</span>{Randomized Trials and CONSORT}<span class="pl-c1">\label</span>{randomized-trials}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1148" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1148"></td>
        <td id="LC1148" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">The most widely adopted reporting standard guideline is the Consolidated Standards of Reporting Trials (<span class="pl-c1">\href</span>{http://www.consort-statement.org}{CONSORT}). Parallel to construction of <span class="pl-c1">\href</span>{http://clinicaltrials.gov}{clinicaltrials.gov} and registration,</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1149" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1149"></td>
        <td id="LC1149" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">reporting standards evolved, and are now nearly universally adopted for randomized trials published in medical journals, required or requested by reviewers during the review process. This is still in its infancy in the social sciences.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1150" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1150"></td>
        <td id="LC1150" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1151" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1151"></td>
        <td id="LC1151" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">The original CONSORT  was developed in the mid 1990&#39;s <span class="pl-c1">\citep</span>{begg_c_improving_1996}. After five years, research showed that reporting of essential details, as required by the checklist, had significantly increased in journals requiring the standard  <span class="pl-c1">\citep</span>{moher_d_use_2001}. The statement was revised in 2001, and simultaneously published in three of the top journals <span class="pl-c1">\citep</span>{moher_consort_2001}). The statement was again revised in 2010 <span class="pl-c1">\citep</span>{schulz_consort_2010}. The statement is a 25-item checklist pertaining to the title, abstract, introduction, methods, results, and discussion of the article in question, and seeks to delineate the minimum requirements of disclosure that may not be sufficiently addressed through other measures.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1152" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1152"></td>
        <td id="LC1152" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1153" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1153"></td>
        <td id="LC1153" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\subsection</span>{Social Science Reporting Standards}<span class="pl-c1">\label</span>{soc-sci-standards}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1154" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1154"></td>
        <td id="LC1154" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">Though a standard akin to CONSORT has not been formally adopted by social science or behavioral science journals, at least as far as we are aware, there have been attempts to do this: In political science, the Experimental Research Section Standards Committee produced a detailed list of items required for disclosure of experiments in political science <span class="pl-c1">\citep</span>{gerber_reporting_????}. This checklist is available <span class="pl-c1">\href</span>{http://www.davidhendry.net/research-supplemental/gerberetal2014-reportingstandards/gerberetal2014-reportingstandards&amp;appendix1.pdf}{here}.<span class="pl-c1">\footnote</span>{<span class="pl-c1">\url</span>{http://www.davidhendry.net/research-supplemental/gerberetal2014-reportingstandards/gerberetal2014-reportingstandards&amp;appendix1.pdf}}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1155" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1155"></td>
        <td id="LC1155" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1156" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1156"></td>
        <td id="LC1156" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">In economics, where no standards have been developed, one article has highlighted the fact that there is not much discussion of essential features of randomization (how was randomization stratified, if at all? How were control variables determined?), but no standards have been adopted. <span class="pl-c1">\citep</span>{bruhn_pursuit_2009}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1157" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1157"></td>
        <td id="LC1157" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1158" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1158"></td>
        <td id="LC1158" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">In psychological and behavioral research, an extention to CONSORT for Social and Psychological Interventions (CONSORT-SPI) has been developed in <span class="pl-c1">\citep</span>{montgomery2013protocol}, but has so far not been widely adopted, or required by journals. </td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1159" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1159"></td>
        <td id="LC1159" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1160" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1160"></td>
        <td id="LC1160" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\subsection</span>{Observational Reporting Standards}<span class="pl-c1">\label</span>{observational-standards}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1161" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1161"></td>
        <td id="LC1161" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">Social science has yet to make a serious push for reporting standards in RCTs, let alone observational work, but the medical/epidemiological literature has created standards in this type of work, though they are not as widely adopted as CONSORT. Perhaps the most well-known is the <span class="pl-c1">\href</span>{http://www.strobe-statement.org}{STROBE Statement} (Strengthening the Reporting of Observational Studies in Epidemiology). STROBE provides checklists for reporting of cohort, case-control, and cross-sectional studies. These standards have been endorsed by approximately 100 journals in the field.<span class="pl-c1">\footnote</span>{<span class="pl-c1">\url</span>{http://www.strobe-statement.org/index.php?id=strobe-endorsement}}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1162" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1162"></td>
        <td id="LC1162" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1163" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1163"></td>
        <td id="LC1163" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">Medicine has in fact come up with too many checklists to describe them all individually. Acknowledging that every field and type of research is different, the Equator Network (Enhancing the Quality of Transparency of Health Research) serves as an umbrella organization that seeks to keep tabs on all the best reporting standards and help researchers find which reporting standard is most relevant for their research. See <span class="pl-c1">\url</span>{http://www.equator-network.org/} for more information.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1164" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1164"></td>
        <td id="LC1164" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1165" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1165"></td>
        <td id="LC1165" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>

</td>
